Earlier on they made a point that the only way to survive is to either succumb to your trauma (kill yourself) or traumatise somebody else (kill somebody infront of a witness), so I think the movie should have ended with Dr. Rose discovering a third option: overcoming her trauma (her mother's death), killing the monster and defeating the curse. I'm kind of a horror movie snob. I've seen A LOT of them. And it takes a lot to scare me. Jump scares don't do it. Slasher flicks I find boring and uninspired. Creative visuals and atmosphere go a LONG way with me. That being said, I've watched pretty much every well reviewed horror movie or show that's come out this October looking for another It Follows or Hereditary and nothing has been able to scratch that itch. This movie definitely starts off like another generic horror movie, but they really surprised me in the end. They absolutely nailed the visuals in this, especially towards the end. I've also noticed that the best horror movies are ones that are metaphors for something people have to deal with in the real world and it's clear that this was a statement on mental illness, highlighting the fact that regardless of whether something someone is seeing or feeling isn't real, it is real enough to them and has enough of an impact that it shouldn't be ignored. They could have been a little more subtle about it though, but I appreciated the message nonetheless.

Just watched the movie, while I don't think it has a great rewatch factor- the smiles won't be as scary- I think it was a great movie to watch in cinema. Spoilers-  The entity at the end is pretty basic and probably the least scary part of the movie but the paranoia of the next camera shot having someone smiling left me covering my eyes most of the time. It is truly uncanny valley. However there are countless needless jumpscares, such as the transitions between scenes- train going past, can opening, door unlocking etc. I'm sure they serve their purpose but it means we loss tension at the end of every scene.   Overall, I'd say worth watching in cinema but not a favourite

I'm a big fan of horror and i was really happy to stumble across this movie. The sad thing about most horror movies is that ocne you see the antagonistic villain/spirt / whatever it is, it isn't as scary anymore since you know what to expect. But with this one, the entity could where anyone's face, so you could never feel secure about the current circumstance you're in. Even during day time where you expect things to be okay, its far from it. There is also the hallucinations which just feel horrifying. You can't tell which reality is real and you experience the constant fright alongside the protagonist trying to discern what's real and what isn't. It's really well done that's for sure.  Inwould advise however not to watch the trailer before watching the movie. I didn't do that and i enjoyed it but after having watched this, it shows a lot of key moments that may kill the surprise.

Alright for real now, I know that everyone is going bonkers about that one scene but the thing is that the movie is still probably gonna be the good ol' "entity chases person for nor exact reason other than funi scream haha". It's overdone, if this film is a success then there is no hope for the horror movie industry. Like, from all of this trailer the only thing you found scary was a jumpscare, bruh, no fucking shit, scream doesen't equal scary.  This is something that really bothers me about horror movies, they make them to be seen by an incredibly stupid audience. This means that theses types of movies tell you exactly what is what, there is no mistery nor interpretation because it's already force fed to you, the human mind fears the unknown, and this entity can be switched with anything and it would make no diference, meaning that it is quite much known.   Actual good horror is stuff like ARG's, mostly done by indie and it is 100% free and available on YT. Stuff like the Mandela Catalogue, Local 68, The Monument Mythos just to name a few. These are good horros that enphasize in the mistery of it, you don't know what is going on so you are scared, and you try to figure it out to reveal scarier layers to the narritive, THAT is true horror.   Not to say every pro horror movie is bad, stuff like Mid Sommar or Heridatary are great movies, that also focuse on the mistery AND explore branches that are usually ignored like cults. In conclusion, fuck this lazy ass written shit this is no horror, it's just a dude putting a air horn in my ear.

The scenes shot upside down in the trailer are referring to the scene at 0:56 that shows the scale of pain patients are in from 1-10. The poster shows an upside down smile on the scale (frown) is the worst kind of pain while a normal smile is no pain. The scenes that are shot upside down are imagery portraying the people who are smiling are actually in the worst kind of pain (according to the poster at 0:56).
